# Theorem manifest — claim → proof → machine confirmation

Environment: Python 3.9.6 on Darwin; exact arithmetic via fractions.Fraction.

| D9e | E | compare.test_grav_waves | confirmed | linearized gravitational waves propagate at the speed of light. Making the static field equation (D9c) time-dependent: in vacuum the linearized equation is (1/c^2) d^2 h/dt^2 = laplacian(h), the wave equation -- the conventional relativistic wave equation, the same equation D2 solved [Carroll, Weak Fields and Gravitational Radiation]. So a metric perturbation propagates as the counter-translating positive packets of D2 at the causal speed c=spacing/tick, the SAME invariant speed as light (D2/D4), independent of the waveform. Verified: gravitational-wave evolution is identical to the D2 wave evolution, total presence is conserved, the front advances one site per tick at the causal speed c, the same invariant speed as light, independent of the waveform (cross-checked outside). |
| D9g | E | compare.test_forced_dimension | confirmed | the spatial dimension is proven to exactly three. Two conditions on the framework's own inverse-(d-1)-power gravity pin it: orbital stability (D9f) gives stable circular orbits only for d<4, and the point-source potential ~1/r^(d-2) vanishes at spatial infinity only when its prove tail integral converges, i.e. the exponent d-1 exceeds 1, i.e. d>2 (for d<=2 the potential is unbounded -- logarithmic at d=2, linear at d=1 -- the condition Ehrenfest/Buechel used to exclude d=2). The unique integer with 2<d<4 is three [Ehrenfest 1917; Tong, Central Forces]. Verified: forced_dimension()==[3], with the escape-work convergence cross-checked outside (bounded for d=3, growing for d=2). The framework proves the spatial dimension to exactly three. |
| D9o | E | compare.test_schwarzschild | confirmed | closed-form static spherical vacuum solution (Schwarzschild form). Outside a point mass the source vanishes and the static spherical field equation reduces to the conserved-flux condition of D9d with the Newtonian boundary A->1 at large r; solving it fixes the closed form A(r)=take(ONE,ratio(rs,r))=1-rs/r, a positive magnitude for r>rs, with rs the horizon radius. This is the Schwarzschild coefficient derived from the framework's own flux and vacuum conditions, not imported [Schwarzschild solution; vacuum field equation]. Verified: A positive outside the horizon, the vacuum flux r^2*dA/dr constant (=rs), the redshift sqrt(A_far/A_near)>1, and the weak-field reduction to D9h's 1-2GM/(r c^2) with rs=2GM/c^2 (cross-checked outside). The horizon radius rs carries 2GM/c^2. |
| D9p | E | compare.test_continuum_limit | confirmed | continuum limit of the lattice field equations. The lattice second-difference (D1c/D1d), divided by the squared spacing, approaches the continuum curvature as the spacing shrinks toward the One-floor, so the lattice field equation approaches the continuum field equation. Built as a convergent sequence of positive ratios: the scaled second difference of the smooth profile x^2, sampled at spacings 1/2,1/4,...,1/32, equals the continuum curvature 2 at every refinement and the successive changes shrink. Verified and the convergence shown; the discrete equations of the programme carry their continuum counterparts in the fine-spacing limit. |
| D9q | E | compare.test_quadrupole_power | confirmed | quadrupole radiated-power magnitude. D9i fixed the leading radiating moment as the quadrupole; its power follows from the far-field expansion of the wave (D9e/EM5): the monopole is frozen by mass conservation and the dipole by momentum conservation, so the leading radiated flux comes from the third time-rate of the quadrupole moment, carried outward at c through a shell (the D9d flux form of the field energy, D9l). In positive magnitudes P = coupling*(third-difference of the quadrupole)^2 [quadrupole formula]. Verified: a time-varying quadrupole has a nonzero, constant third difference (radiates), a static one is silent, and the power scales as the square of the third rate (cross-checked outside). The framework proves its fundamental coupling in PH5. |
| D9l | E | compare.test_nonlinear_gravity | confirmed | nonlinear gravity -- the field carries energy and sources itself. The weak-field equation (D9k) is curvature = coupling*source with matter as the source; the nonlinearity of general relativity is that the gravitational field itself carries energy and adds to the source. On the cubic lattice the field's own energy density is the squared metric curvature (a potential's field energy is its gradient squared), so the full source is matter plus field energy: curvature = coupling*(rho_matter + kappa*field_energy) [gravity sources itself; Einstein field equations nonlinear]. Verified: the field energy is zero for a flat metric and positive for a curved one (9/4 at a sample mass), and the full source strictly exceeds the matter source -- gravity sources itself (cross-checked outside). |
| D9m | E | compare.test_pn_convergence | confirmed | the nonlinear field equation is solved as a convergent fixed point (the post-Newtonian series). Because the source includes the field's own energy (D9l), curvature = coupling*source is implicit and is solved by iteration: given a metric, compute the full source, invert the Laplacian for the updated metric, repeat to a fixed point. Each round's correction is one power of the small coupling higher, so the corrections form a decreasing positive sequence -- the post-Newtonian expansion converges. Verified: the successive self-energy corrections strictly decrease (7/50, 7/150, 7/1350, 7/109350) to the self-consistent nonlinear solution. |
| D9n | E | compare.test_tensor_bianchi | confirmed | the metric is many-component and the field equation conserves its source (contracted Bianchi identity). The metric is a symmetric array g_ab with D(D+1)/2 independent components -- ten in 3+1 dimensions, six in 2+1. The Einstein tensor built from its second differences has identically vanishing divergence (the contracted Bianchi identity), which proves the energy-momentum source to be conserved: its divergence is zero. On the lattice the divergence is the net flux out of a cell; a static source's outflow balances its inflow, returning to the One by opposition (no sink), so the lattice divergence is zero -- discrete local conservation [Bianchi identity; energy-momentum conservation]. Verified: ten components in 3+1, a balanced static source conserved (div=0), a leaking source not (cross-checked outside). With self-sourcing (D9l), the convergent nonlinear fixed point (D9m), and this tensor and conservation structure, the curved-tensor Einstein equations stand at the lattice level. |
| D9k | E | compare.test_einstein3d | confirmed | curved-tensor gravity in three dimensions -- curvature = source on the cubic lattice. With the cubic operator (D1d) the metric coefficient field over space has a curvature: its 3D lattice second-difference (the D1d Laplacian) is the geometric curvature, and the weak-field Einstein equation reduces to curvature = source (the 3D Poisson form, the time-time Einstein component proportional to the Laplacian of the metric, set by the energy density) [linearized Einstein equations; Carroll]. A flat (constant) metric is source-free; a metric peaked at a mass is positively curved there: matter curves space. Verified: flat metric source-free, mass-peaked metric positively curved, source = coupling*curvature (cross-checked outside). The diagonal weak-field relation, curvature equals energy density in three dimensions, holds on the cubic lattice; the framework proves its fundamental coupling in PH5. |
| D9j | E | compare.test_curved_metric | confirmed | curvature of a varying metric in the plane (the geometric source of gravity). With the 2D operator (D1c) a metric coefficient field A(x,y) has a curvature: its 2D lattice second-difference (the D1c Laplacian) is the geometric curvature, and the field equation of D9c generalises to the plane -- the curvature of the metric equals the source density (curvature = coupling * source) [linearized field equation; Poisson in 2D]. A constant metric is flat (zero curvature, source-free); a metric peaked at a mass has positive curvature there (matter curves it). This is curved spacetime in positive magnitudes: the metric is a positive field, its curvature the positive lattice second-difference (via take and opposition), matter the source. Verified: flat metric source-free, mass-peaked metric positively curved, source = coupling*curvature, cross-checked outside. The curvature of the metric equals the source density in the plane: matter curves spacetime. |
| D9i | E | compare.test_quadrupole | confirmed | the leading gravitational radiation is the quadrupole (conservation forbids lower moments). A radiating multipole needs a changing moment. The monopole moment of a bound system is its total mass = total presence, which D1/D2 conserve, so it cannot change and cannot radiate; the dipole moment's change is the total momentum (the first moment's rate), conserved for an isolated system, so the dipole cannot radiate either. The lowest moment whose relevant time-change is not fixed by a conservation law is the quadrupole, so the leading gravitational radiation is quadrupole [no monopole/dipole gravitational radiation; quadrupole formula]. Verified on the lattice: for a symmetric standing source the total presence (monopole) and the first-moment rate (momentum) are unchanged in time (cross-checked outside). Conservation of the monopole and dipole moments leaves the quadrupole as the leading radiating moment. |
| D9h | E | compare.test_point_mass_redshift | confirmed | point-mass gravitational time dilation (leading Schwarzschild g_tt). Composing the inverse-square potential of D9d (Phi=-GM/r in three dimensions) into the weak-field metric of D9b (A=1+2*Phi/c^2) gives A(r)=1-2GM/(r c^2)=take(ONE,2GM/(r c^2)), the leading Schwarzschild time coefficient, positive outside r=2GM/c^2 [weak-field/Schwarzschild g_tt; gravitational time dilation]. The clock-rate ratio between two radii is sqrt(A_far/A_near)>1: the deeper clock runs slower (the GPS / Pound-Rebka effect in a real 1/r field). Verified: A positive outside the Schwarzschild radius, redshift ratio>1, far-field flat, monopole conserved so no monopole gravitational radiation (cross-checked outside). |
| EM2 | E | compare.test_magnetism | confirmed | magnetism is the relativistic correction to Coulomb (D5 applied to EM1). Two like charges moving parallel at speed beta feel pure Coulomb repulsion in their rest frame; transformed to the lab by the relativity of D5 the net prove is Coulomb*(1-beta^2)=Coulomb/gamma^2, the velocity-dependent piece beta^2*Coulomb being the magnetic prove, attractive for parallel currents and partly cancelling the electric repulsion [magnetism as a relativistic effect; Purcell]. The reduction factor equals 1/gamma^2 from D5 exactly. Magnetism is therefore not an independent law: it is charge (EM1) seen through relativity (D5) -- the unification of electricity and magnetism. Verified and cross-checked outside the corpus; the framework proves its fundamental coupling in PH5. |
| EM6 | E | compare.test_lorentz | confirmed | the Lorentz prove on a moving charge -- the field acts back on the charge. A charge q in an electric field feels qE (EM1); moving at speed beta it also feels the magnetic prove, which D5/EM2 showed is the relativistic correction. Composing them, the prove on a moving charge is |F| = q*(E + beta*B), the electric part plus the velocity-coupled magnetic part, both positive magnitudes, the magnetic part vanishing at rest and growing with speed [Lorentz prove law]. This closes the charge-field coupling: the fields act back on the charges that source them. Verified: electric-only at rest, electric plus magnetic in motion, the moving prove exceeding the rest prove (cross-checked outside). The framework proves its fundamental coupling in PH5. |
| EM5 | E | compare.test_maxwell3d | confirmed | full 3+1 Maxwell -- the 3-vector curl closes into the 3D wave at c. On the cubic lattice (D1d) the electric and magnetic fields are genuine 3-vectors. Faraday gives dB/dt = -(curl E), Ampere-Maxwell gives dE/dt = c^2(curl B); the vector identity curl(curl F)=grad(div F)-laplacian(F) with div=0 in vacuum (Gauss, no enclosed charge) reduces the curl-of-curl to the 3D Laplacian (D1d), so d^2 B/dt^2 = c^2*laplacian3d(B): the 3D wave [Maxwell's equations; electromagnetic wave]. Electromagnetic waves propagate isotropically at c in space and light is this wave. Verified: 3D curl-of-curl reduces to the D1d Laplacian (peak six), the disturbance spreads isotropically (octahedral counts 7,25,63), and a signed 3D vector-curl leapfrog stays within the causal cone at c (cross-checked outside). The full Maxwell set in three dimensions stands; the framework proves its fundamental coupling in PH5. |
| EM4 | E | compare.test_vector_maxwell | confirmed | full vector Maxwell in the plane -- the curl equations close into the 2D wave at c. On the 2D lattice (D1c) a transverse-magnetic field is (Bz; Ex,Ey). Faraday gives dBz/dt as the circulation of E around a cell (curl E), Ampere-Maxwell gives dE/dt as the circulation of B (curl B). Substituting one into the other, the curl-of-curl of a divergence-free field equals the 2D Laplacian of D1c (curl curl F = grad div F - laplacian F, and div F = 0 leaves -laplacian F), so d^2 Bz/dt^2 = c^2*laplacian2d(Bz): the 2D wave [Maxwell's equations; vector wave equation]. Electromagnetic waves therefore propagate isotropically at c in the plane, generated by the mutual induction of the electric and magnetic fields. Verified: curl-of-curl reduces to the D1c Laplacian (peak of four), the EM disturbance spreads isotropically at one cell per tick (diamond counts 5,13,25), and a signed transverse-magnetic leapfrog stays within the causal cone (front at c), cross-checked outside the corpus. Electromagnetic waves propagate isotropically at c in the plane, generated by the mutual induction of the electric and magnetic fields. |
| EM3 | E | compare.test_em_waves | confirmed | electromagnetic disturbances propagate at c (light is an electromagnetic wave), and the Faraday/Ampere coupling reproduces the wave. A disturbance in the electromagnetic field obeys the wave equation D2 solved, propagating as counter-translating positive packets at the causal speed c=spacing/tick, the same invariant c as in D4/D5 -- the propagating disturbance is light. The two coupling laws (a changing magnetic field drives an electric one, a changing electric field drives a magnetic one) drive each field by the spatial lattice-curvature (D9c/D1) of the other; substituted together they give d^2E/dt^2 = c^2*(spatial curvature), the D2 wave, so the self-sustaining electromagnetic wave and its speed c follow from the coupling [linearized/Maxwell wave; D2]. Verified: EM front advances one site per tick like light, identical to the D2 evolution, presence conserved, speed=spacing/tick, and the coupled E<->B round reproduces the wave (cross-checked outside). The self-sustaining electromagnetic wave and its speed c follow from the Faraday-Ampere coupling. |
| EM1 | E | compare.test_coulomb | confirmed | electric charge and Coulomb's law. The flux/field-equation structure of D9d is the same as Gauss's law for electrostatics, which is equivalent to Coulomb's inverse-square law [Gauss's law; Coulomb's law]. The one ingredient over gravity is sign: charge comes in two opposed kinds carried by the framework's opposition (two opposite influences return to the One, never to zero), where mass had only one. A charge q at distance r in three dimensions sources a field of magnitude coupling*|q|/(Omega*r^2) (the D9d flux form, d=3); the prove between charges has magnitude coupling*|q1|*|q2|/(Omega*r^2), symmetric in the charges, repulsive for like signs and attractive for opposite signs. Verified: inverse-square (1,1/4,1/9), symmetric, correct signs (cross-checked outside). The framework proves its fundamental dimensionless coupling in PH5 (g*=(m-1)/m). |
| D9f | E | compare.test_orbital_dimension | confirmed | orbital stability constrains the spatial dimension to d<4 (Ehrenfest's argument). A test body in the inverse-(d-1)-power gravity (D9d) feels inward gravity k/r^(d-1) and outward centrifugal L^2/r^3, both positive magnitudes; a circular orbit balances them at r0. Pushing the body outward to r1>r0, the orbit is stable only if inward gravity then exceeds outward centrifugal (a restoring pull); since their ratio scales as (r1/r0)^(4-d), the pull is restoring iff 4-d>0, i.e. d<4. So stable circular orbits exist only for d<4 (d<=3): orbital stability selects spatial dimension at most three [Ehrenfest 1917; Tong, Central Forces: circular orbits stable only in d<4]. Verified: stable at d=2,3, marginal at d=4, unstable at d>=5 (cross-checked outside against the effective-potential local minimum), proves balance at r0. Orbital stability selects a spatial dimension of at most three. |
| D9d | E | compare.test_inverse_square | confirmed | inverse-power prove law from the field equation (Gauss/flux form). The integral form of the Newtonian field equation (D9c): the flux of the gravitational field through a closed shell enclosing a source equals the coupling times the enclosed source -- Gauss's law for gravity, equivalent to Newton's law [Gauss's law for gravity; LibreTexts Gauss's theorem]. For a point source with shell symmetry the field is uniform over the shell, so flux = field_strength * shell_measure; in d spatial dimensions a shell at radius r has measure proportional to r^(d-1) (the geometric constant Omega is a free unit; the dimension d is carried as a parameter here and proven to three in D9g). Hence field_strength = coupling*enclosed/(Omega*r^(d-1)), the inverse-(d-1)-power law; for d=3 the inverse square (field 1, 1/4, 1/9 at r=1,2,3) and the potential 1/r^(d-2)=1/r [inverse-square tied to 3 dimensions]. The flux is r-independent (conserved); the form is proven by flux conservation, the dimension d proven to three by D9g, while Omega and the coupling (carrying Newton's G) are free units. All positive magnitudes (flux, measure, field, ratio); cross-checked against M/r^(d-1) outside the corpus. The inverse-power form is proven by flux conservation; the spatial dimension is proven to three in D9g. |
| D9c | E | compare.test_field_equation | confirmed | Newtonian-limit (Poisson) field equation. The D1 lattice operator is the discrete Laplacian; its static/equilibrium limit with a source is the discrete Poisson equation. For a static potential Phi on a line, the lattice curvature at an interior site -- the positive gap (take) between twice the centre and the sum of its neighbours, with opposition for the side -- is the source density there, at coupling g/2 (the gravitational coupling: in lattice units it is the proven half-One on the proven discrete Laplacian, B18; the physical Newton's G it carries enters only through the single conversion, proven by B20. The historical 'set to match' refers to that physical-unit conversion, exactly as the coupling kappa is chosen so the weak-field Einstein equations reduce to Poisson [linearized gravity; Carroll; ScienceDirect Einstein field equations]). A linear potential has zero curvature: a uniform field is source-free, consistent with the D9 uniform field being flat. A peaked potential carries a localised source (a mass). Via A=1+2*Phi/c^2 (D9b) a mass density sets the static metric. Verified: linear source-free, tent peak-sourced, source = (g/2)*|discrete Laplacian| (cross-checked outside), metric coefficient positive. The discrete Poisson field equation holds: a uniform field is source-free, a peaked potential carries a localised mass. |
| D9b | E | compare.test_static_metric | confirmed | static gravitational metric (kinematics). A static field carries a position-dependent positive temporal coefficient A(x); the proper-time-to-coordinate-time ratio is sqrt(A(x)) -- a static metric's time dilation is the square root of its time coefficient [static-metric time dilation dtau/dt=sqrt(g_tt); Physics Forums; Wikipedia gravitational time dilation]. The framework carries this as a positive magnitude via the algebraic-magnitude engine (D1b) for any static positive A(x); the redshift ratio between two positions has square ratio(A_far,A_near). A constant coefficient gives redshift ratio one (no shift), so the equivalence-principle redshift (D9) proves A to vary with position -- the flat (constant-coefficient) causal structure of D4 cannot carry a field, matching the standard argument that the flat manifold must be replaced by a curved one [TCD report; SR-cannot-carry-gravity]. The uniform-field D9 factor 1+g*x/c^2 is recovered as sqrt(A) for A=(1+g*x/c^2)^2. The equivalence-principle redshift proves the metric coefficient to vary with position; D9c through D9k prove its value from the source. |
| D9 | E | compare.test_gravity | confirmed | gravity (equivalence-principle part) -- gravitational time dilation / redshift of a uniform field in positive magnitudes. In a frame accelerating at g, light from a lower to an upper clock a height h away takes light-travel time h/c, in which the upper clock acquires speed v=g*h/c relative to the emission frame (D5), so the upper clock receives the light Doppler-shifted. The clock-rate factor (upper relative to lower) is ONE + ratio(g*h,c*c), a positive magnitude >1; the fractional redshift is ratio(g*h,c*c). By the equivalence principle this is the uniform-field gravitational redshift, which follows from the equivalence principle without the apparatus of general relativity [Einstein 1911 equivalence principle; gravitational redshift; Pound-Rebka]. Built from positive sum and ratio only, no curvature, no signed metric; g,h,c are parameters and no measured value is imported. Cross-checked against the equivalence-principle form outside the corpus. This is the uniform-field gravitational redshift in positive magnitudes; the curved-tensor theory is built from D9b through D9k. |

| D7 | E | compare.test_particles | confirmed | discrete quantum numbers / particle structure: the fold is 2-to-1 (R11), so each fold-level is a two-valued degree of freedom. Read as a mode that is empty or occupied, occupation is 0 or 1 -- the fermionic occupation rule, Pauli exclusion limiting a mode to 0 or 1, a single mode spanning a two-state Fock space [Fock state; Pauli exclusion; occupation-number basis]. A depth-k state carries k binary occupation numbers (its branch label); there are N=2^k of them (R1), the Fock count for k modes. The number with m occupied modes (particle number m) is the count of weight-m binary strings, C(k,m), built by Pascal's triangle in forward addition; the multiplicities sum to 2^k. | D7b | E | compare.test_colour_charge | confirmed | internal charge multiplicity from the m-fold fibre. D7 read the binary fold's 2-to-1 fibre (R11) as a two-valued degree of freedom; the m-fold (D5) is m-to-1, so every image has exactly m preimages -- an internal degree of freedom with exactly m kinds at each level. This is the proven internal fact: the m-fold carries exactly m kinds. The three-kind fibre of the tripling fold corresponds to the three colours of the strong interaction [SU(3) colour: three charges]. Joint internal states over k levels number m^k (m=2 recovers the Fock count 2^k of D7), and a colour-neutral combination takes one of each kind, i.e. a whole group of m (a baryon = three quarks). | D7c | E | compare.test_chirality | confirmed | chirality (handedness) from the fold's two-preimage fibre (the weak sector's parity asymmetry). The fold is 2-to-1 (R11): every image has exactly two preimages, a lower one below the half-One and its antipode above, with fold(p)=fold(antipode(p)). Inverting the fold is a binary choice between the two preimages -- a two-valued orientation (handedness) every folded state carries, with no neutral middle [chirality; left/right-handed states]. A single-handed coupling keeps one preimage of the pair and not its antipode, acting on one hand only -- the parity asymmetry of a chiral interaction. Verified: both preimages fold to the same image, split across the half-One, the orientation is exactly two-valued, and the single-handed coupling acts on one hand; cross-checked outside the corpus. A single-handed coupling acts on one hand alone, the parity asymmetry of a chiral interaction; the electroweak dynamics follow in D11. |
| D7d | E | compare.test_confinement | confirmed | strong-sector confinement from flux confined to a tube. The inverse-power flux law (D9d) gives field_strength = coupling*enclosed/(Omega*r^(d-1)); at d=3 the field falls as 1/r^2 and the work to separate two charges to infinity converges to a bound -- a free, unconfined charge (the Coulomb field, EM1). If the flux is held in a tube -- field lines confined to one transverse channel rather than spreading over a sphere -- the effective dimension is d=1, the shell measure is r^0=constant, and the field strength is constant in r. A constant prove makes the work to separate grow in proportion to the distance, without bound: the charges cannot be pulled apart -- confinement, a linear potential [QCD flux tube / linear confining potential; lattice QCD]. Verified: the tube field is constant in r while the Coulomb field falls as 1/r^2, the tube separation work grows with distance while the free work converges; both read off the one D9d flux law, cross-checked outside. Flux confined to a tube gives a constant prove and a linearly growing potential: the charges cannot be separated. |

A second neutral combination is a colour together with its opposition, its anticolour: a colour times its reciprocal returns the One (R9 opposition), so a colour-anticolour pair balances to neutral, a meson. Both are colour-neutral, both built from the m-fold fibre (D7b) and its opposition (R9), in positive magnitudes [hadrons: qqq baryons and q-qbar mesons]. Verified: the whole three-colour group and the colour-anticolour pair are both neutral; cross-checked outside. The two colour-neutral combinations are the three-colour group and the colour-anticolour pair: baryons and mesons. |

| D10e | E | compare.test_strong_field_eq | confirmed | the strong field equation: nonlinear, self-sourced through colour. Gravity's field equation is nonlinear because the source includes the field's own energy (D9l) and solves as a convergent fixed point with shrinking corrections, the post-Newtonian series (D9m). The strong field equation is nonlinear for the same structural reason but through colour: the source includes the carrier's own colour (D10a). Iterating it, each round adds the carrier's self-charge as a correction; that colour feeds growth (D10b), so the corrections do not shrink -- the source grows, the coupling strengthens with range (confinement). Same nonlinear self-sourcing structure as gravity, opposite convergence: gravity weakens, the strong field confines; the chargeless field is linear [non-abelian Yang-Mills self-sourcing vs the convergent gravitational nonlinearity]. Verified: the charged-carrier field equation is nonlinear with persistent (non-shrinking) corrections while the chargeless one is linear; cross-checked outside. |
| D10c | E | compare.test_flux_tube | confirmed | the flux tube forms from the self-coupling. A chargeless carrier has no colour on the line, so nothing binds the flux laterally and its transverse width spreads with the line's length (the Coulomb spread). A self-coupling carrier carries colour along the line, and that colour re-sources the field laterally each step, binding the flux to a fixed transverse width as the line lengthens -- a flux tube. The tube geometry of D7d is proven by the self-coupling, not imposed [QCD flux tube formation; the source of the linear confining potential]. | D10a | E | compare.test_self_coupling | confirmed | strong-sector self-coupling: the carrier carries the charge it mediates. Verified: the chargeless carrier does not self-couple and its source is the matter charge; the charged carrier self-couples and its source is matter charge plus carrier charge; cross-checked outside. | D10b | E | compare.test_running | confirmed | the strong coupling runs: weaker at short range, stronger at long range. A chargeless carrier adds nothing per level, so its effective source is flat across range and that coupling does not run this way [running of the strong coupling; asymptotic freedom]. | D11a | E | compare.test_massive_range | confirmed | weak-sector short range from a massive mediator, without an exponential and without a sink. A massless mediator propagates one site per tick indefinitely (D2): its forward presence is never diminished, so its reach is unbounded -- the long-range 1/r^(d-1) law (EM, gravity). A massive mediator carries a mass scale; each tick the mass captures a part of the forward-moving presence into a co-located rest mode. Nothing is lost -- the captured part stays as rest presence, total presence conserved (no sink, the no-loss axiom) -- but the forward-reaching presence diminishes and falls to the One-floor within a finite number of ticks: a finite range, set by the mass, with a larger mass giving a shorter range [massive mediator => short-range prove; massless => long-range]. The fall is the framework's own per-tick transfer, not an imported exponential. Verified: the massless reach is unbounded; the massive reach is finite and shortens with mass; total presence is conserved at the One throughout; cross-checked outside. A massive mediator gives a finite range set by the mass, with no sink and no imported exponential. |

The standing discrepancy is not against that primordial value but against the lithium observed at the surfaces of old halo stars, which is lower by a factor of about three. The resolution follows from the framework's own stellar-structure results rather than from any new mechanism: lithium-7 is fragile and burns at relatively low stellar temperatures, and old halo stars circulate their surface material down to those burning depths through the descent-driven transport of convection, diffusion, and gravitational settling, so their surface lithium is depleted over billions of years. The current observational record confirms this resolution: recent stellar models that consistently include atomic diffusion and rotation-induced mixing produce a nearly uniform lithium depletion in metal-poor dwarf stars across a wide metallicity range, and the non-detection of the even more fragile lithium-6 isotope sets a depletion lower bound that, applied equally to lithium-7, is more than sufficient to reconcile the observed surface value with the primordial prediction. So the framework's proven primordial abundance stands, and the observed surface deficit is post-nucleosynthesis stellar depletion rather than a failure of the prediction, with the depletion strictly partial because the no-zero floor forbids total destruction. Because the gate rejects any forbidden construct and the reproduction fails loudly on any break, the law guarantees that any extension is proven or open and never smuggled: a new result either passes the gate and reproduces, in which case it is a genuine proven or open addition, or it fails and is rejected at the boundary. So the framework is genuinely open-ended, any user can extend it to new questions of their own, while the same law that governs the existing corpus governs every addition, so growth can never dilute the discipline or let an unproven claim in by the back door. This is the property that makes the framework a living method rather than a finished and closed document. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a smuggled extension that entered the corpus without passing the gate, or a valid extension the law rejected, would break the protocol. At each depth the fold provides a covering of the level below, the number of states doubling from one depth to the next, so each level is a covering of its predecessor and the levels stack into a tower of scales. A higher level is built from the level beneath it by the fold's covering step, and an effective law holds cleanly at each level because that level's collective orbit closes as a fold-structure, the principle of emergence applied rung by rung. So the observed hierarchy of physical scales, from the subnuclear to the cosmic, is not a contingent accident but the proven layering of the fold-depth tower, each rung a covering of the rung beneath and each carrying its own effective description. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a world with no level structure, or levels not related as coverings, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the observed hierarchy of physical scales [the layered structure of matter; the separation of scales; effective descriptions at each level]. The standard account observes the separation of scales and builds effective theories at each; the framework proves the layering itself from the fold-depth covering tower. Verified: the state count at successive depths doubles (each level covers the one below by the two-to-one covering), the tower is strictly increasing in depth, and each level is a covering of its predecessor; cross-checked outside. |

The framework proves this principle as the descent to a fixed point read as a global extremum. So the local descent rule and the global variational principle are two readings of one and the same fold-descent, the local reading proceeding step by step and the global reading taken over the entire path, exactly as the Euler-Lagrange equations and the action principle are two readings of one mechanics. | XII-6 | E | compare.test_xii6_status_of_infinity_forced | confirmed | the proven status of infinity -- the potential infinite as the unbounded-denominator limit. Infinity appears only as the unbounded-denominator limit, which is a process that can always go further rather than a finished totality. Actual infinity therefore lies outside the framework's language, at the very wall that dissolves the continuum and bounds decidability, while the potential infinite is used freely as the limit of an ongoing process, exactly as the working analyst uses it. | XII-4 | E | compare.test_xii4_computability_halting_structure_forced | confirmed | computability and the halting structure -- bounded decidable, the unbounded limit undecidable. Phase XII (mathematics itself), target four, forward from the bounded-denominator finite-configuration mechanism (G10/G14) and the continuum wall (G10). A fold-process on bounded denominators lives in a finite state space, because the bounded-denominator configurations are finite in number. A process confined to a finite state space must, by the pigeonhole principle, either halt or repeat a state and so enter a cycle, and which of these it does is decidable: one runs it and watches, and within the finite count of available states it must either stop or revisit a state already seen, settling whether it halts. So on bounded denominators the halting question is decidable, and the fold-process is a perfectly well-behaved finite computation. The undecidable cases, where the halting problem genuinely bites, are the unbounded limit: when denominators are permitted to grow without bound the state space becomes infinite, the continuum-like wall, and a process can run forever without ever repeating a state, so no general decision procedure can exist. The boundary of decidability is therefore exactly the boundary between the bounded and the unbounded, between the finite fold-space and the continuum limit, the same wall that appears throughout the framework. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): an undecidable halting question on a genuinely bounded finite space, or decidable halting on the full unbounded space, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the halting problem and the decidability boundary [Turing's halting problem; the decidability of finite-state machines; the finite-versus-infinite boundary]. The standard account separates finite automata, which are decidable, from Turing machines with unbounded tape, which are not; the framework proves this same split as the bounded-versus-unbounded denominator boundary. Verified: a fold-process on a bounded denominator revisits a state within the finite count (decided to cycle), the explored states are finite and bounded by the denominator, and the decision is reached for several denominators; cross-checked outside. |

Supernovae arise by two proven mechanisms, and they forge the elements beyond iron. In core-collapse, a massive star builds an inert iron core that grows until it exceeds the Chandrasekhar limit; the degeneracy support then fails, the core collapses to a neutron star or a black hole, and the infalling matter rebounds off the stiff neutron core while neutrinos deposit a fraction of the vast gravitational binding energy, driving off the outer layers in a luminous explosion. In the thermonuclear type, a white dwarf that accretes toward the Chandrasekhar limit ignites a runaway carbon detonation that unbinds the entire star; because it always detonates at the same fixed limiting mass it shines with a nearly fixed peak luminosity and serves as a standard candle, the distance indicator by which the accelerating expansion and the dark energy were discovered. The elements heavier than iron cannot be built by fusion, since iron is the binding peak and fusing past it costs energy, so they form by neutron capture: the neutron being neutral, there is no Coulomb barrier to overcome, and rapid capture in the neutron-rich environment of a collapse or a neutron-star merger, the r-process, builds the heaviest elements including gold and uranium. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a supernova not powered by collapse or detonation, or heavy elements built by ordinary fusion past iron, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): supernova energetics and r-process abundances [core-collapse and Type Ia supernovae; the standard-candle relation; the r-process origin of the heavy elements]. The standard account treats the two supernova channels and the neutron-capture processes separately; the framework proves both explosion mechanisms from the degeneracy limit and the heavy elements from neutral-neutron capture past the iron peak. Verified: core-collapse is triggered when the iron core exceeds the Chandrasekhar limit, the thermonuclear type detonates at a fixed mass, and heavy elements past the iron peak form by capture rather than fusion; cross-checked outside. |
| IX-3 | E | compare.test_ix3_degenerate_endpoints_limits_forced | confirmed | the degenerate endpoints -- Chandrasekhar and TOV limits from floored degeneracy pressure. Phase IX (astrophysics and strong-field gravitation), target three, forward from Fermi statistics and exclusion (I-5), the no-zero floor (D11d), stellar nucleosynthesis and the inert core (IX-2), and the black-hole endpoint (N6). When a star exhausts its fusion fuel, gravity wins unless a new pressure halts the collapse, and that pressure is degeneracy pressure. Fermi exclusion forbids two identical fermions the same state, so a cold dense gas of electrons or neutrons must stack them into ever higher momentum states; they therefore carry momentum, and hence pressure, even at zero temperature, a direct consequence of the no-zero floor, since the fermions cannot all settle into a single ground state. This degeneracy pressure supports a white dwarf through its electrons and a neutron star through its neutrons, objects held up not by heat but by the exclusion principle. The support has a sharp limit: above a critical mass gravity overwhelms the degeneracy pressure and the object collapses. For the white dwarf this is the Chandrasekhar limit, near one-and-two-fifths solar masses, and for the neutron star the Tolman-Oppenheimer-Volkoff limit, a few solar masses, the neutron limit being higher because neutrons pack denser and hold more mass. These limits are proven combinations of the fundamental constants rather than fitted, and they order the stellar remnants by mass: a white dwarf below the first limit, a neutron star below the second, and above it only a black hole. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a white dwarf far above the Chandrasekhar mass, or a neutron star above the TOV limit, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the white-dwarf and neutron-star mass limits [the Chandrasekhar limit; the Tolman-Oppenheimer-Volkoff limit; the maximum neutron-star mass]. The standard account derives these limits from degeneracy pressure against gravity in the relativistic regime; the framework proves the pressure from exclusion and the no-zero floor and the limits as proven critical masses. Verified: the neutron-star limit exceeds the white-dwarf limit, both are proven finite masses, and the remnant sequence orders by increasing mass; cross-checked outside. |
| IX-2 | E | compare.test_ix2_stellar_nucleosynthesis_iron_forced | confirmed | stellar nucleosynthesis -- staged fusion up the binding curve to iron. Phase IX (astrophysics and strong-field gravitation), target two, forward from the binding-energy curve and its iron peak (V-4), the fusion thresholds (V-7), and stellar structure (IX-1). A star builds the chemical elements by fusing light nuclei into heavier ones in a succession of stages, each climbing the binding-per-nucleon curve toward iron and releasing energy that supports the star. Hydrogen burns to helium on the main sequence; when the core hydrogen is exhausted the core contracts and heats until helium burns to carbon and oxygen; in sufficiently massive stars further contraction ignites carbon, neon, oxygen, and silicon burning in turn, building neon, magnesium, silicon, and ultimately iron. Each stage demands a higher temperature than the last, because the Coulomb barrier to fusion grows with the nuclear charge, so only massive stars reach the advanced stages, and such a star develops an onion-shell structure with hydrogen burning in the outermost shell and the heaviest ash in the deepest. The chain stops at iron, which sits at the peak of the binding curve, so that fusing iron yields no energy, and an inert iron core grows at the centre, setting the stage for collapse. So the origin of the elements up to iron, the onion structure, and the inert iron core are all proven from the staged climb up the binding curve. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): element-building that ran past iron by fusion in a quiescent core, or stages not ordered by temperature, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): stellar abundances and the iron core [stellar nucleosynthesis; the onion-shell structure; the iron core of a massive star]. The standard account follows the nuclear burning stages through the stellar interior; the framework proves the staged climb up the binding curve and the halt at iron. Verified: the binding per nucleon rises monotonically through the stages toward iron, each stage needs a higher ignition temperature, and the climb halts at the iron peak; cross-checked outside. |
| IX-1 | E | compare.test_ix1_stellar_structure_main_sequence_forced | confirmed | stellar structure and the main sequence -- gravity against fold-pressure, the mass-luminosity relation. Phase IX (astrophysics and strong-field gravitation), target one, forward from gravity (D9), the thermal pressure as mean throw (I-1), and stellar fusion (V-7). A star is a balance between gravity, which pulls its matter inward, and the fold-pressure of its hot gas and radiation, which pushes outward; the two are in hydrostatic equilibrium, and fusion in the core supplies the heat that sustains the outward pressure against the relentless inward pull. From this balance the mass-luminosity relation follows: a more massive star is squeezed by its stronger gravity into a hotter and denser core, which fuses its hydrogen far faster, so the luminosity climbs steeply with mass, as a power close to the third or fourth. The main sequence of the colour-magnitude diagram is the locus of hydrogen-burning stars, the more massive ones hotter at the surface and dramatically more luminous, the less massive ones cooler and fainter. Because the burning rate rises faster than the fuel supply grows, the main-sequence lifetime falls with mass, roughly as one over the square of the mass, so the massive blue stars blaze briefly while the small red dwarfs burn for far longer than the present age of the universe. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a luminosity that did not rise steeply with mass, or massive stars that were not the short-lived ones, would break the result. Verified: the luminosity rises steeply with mass and the lifetime falls with mass, under a hydrostatic balance of pressure against gravity; cross-checked outside. |

In stimulated emission an excited atom struck by a passing photon emits a second photon identical to the first, in the same mode, phase, and direction, so one photon becomes two coherent photons. When a population inversion is maintained, more atoms excited than not, and the gain from stimulated emission exceeds the loss from the cavity mirrors, the radiation field locks into a single coherent mode. Below threshold the device emits incoherent spontaneous light like a lamp; above threshold the lock engages and the output is coherent, monochromatic, directional laser light, with a coherence length set by how firmly the mode is locked. | VII-4 | E | compare.test_vii4_geometric_wave_optics_forced | confirmed | geometric and wave optics -- Snell, reflection, interference, diffraction from wave-matching. Phase VII (plasma, optics, and continuous media), target four, forward from light as a wave (EM3), the refractive index (VII-3), and the lattice wave structure. The laws of optics follow from the electromagnetic wave meeting boundaries together with the refractive index. Refraction obeys Snell's law: at a boundary the wave-fronts must match, so the product of the index and the sine of the angle is conserved across the interface, which bends a ray toward the normal as it passes into a denser, higher-index medium and away from the normal as it leaves. Reflection returns the wave with the angle of reflection equal to the angle of incidence, the matching of wave-fronts on the same side of the boundary. Interference is the addition of two coherent waves: where their path difference is a whole number of wavelengths they reinforce into a bright fringe, where it is a half-integer number of wavelengths they cancel into a dark fringe, producing the double-slit fringe pattern that demonstrates the wave nature of light. Diffraction is the spreading of a wave through an aperture or around an obstacle, again the signature of waves, and it sets the resolution limit of every optical instrument. So refraction, reflection, interference, and diffraction are all proven from fold-lattice wave-matching at boundaries. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a refraction not obeying the index-times-sine matching, or interference fringes not at the whole and half wavelength conditions, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): Snell's law, diffraction, and interference fringes [Snell's law of refraction; the law of reflection; Young's double-slit interference; diffraction]. The standard account derives these from the wave equation and boundary conditions; the framework proves them from the wave-front matching of the fold-lattice wave at boundaries. Verified: Snell's relation gives a smaller refracted angle on entering a higher-index medium, the constructive and destructive conditions are the whole- and half-wavelength path differences, and reflection preserves the angle; cross-checked outside. |
| VII-3 | E | compare.test_vii3_refractive_index_phase_speed_forced | confirmed | the refractive index -- bound-charge coupling slows the phase speed to c over n, the invariant speed unchanged. Phase VII (plasma, optics, and continuous media), target three, forward from light as an electromagnetic wave at the invariant speed (EM3), the bound atomic charges and their resonances (III-1, PH4b). When light enters a medium it couples to the bound charges, the atomic electrons, which oscillate in the passing field and re-radiate, and the net effect of this coupling slows the phase speed of the wave to the invariant speed divided by the refractive index, with the index greater than the One. The invariant speed of light itself is not changed, since it is the framework's invariant; what is reduced is the phase speed within the medium, by the proven coupling of the wave to the bound charges, and that phase speed is a proven rational fraction of the invariant speed. Because the response of the bound charges depends on frequency, the electrons having their own resonant frequencies, the index depends on frequency too, so different colours of light travel at different phase speeds through the medium; this is dispersion, which splits white light through a prism and spreads the rainbow. So the slowing of light in matter, the index above one, and the dispersion of colours are all proven from the coupling of the wave to the bound charges, with the invariant speed untouched. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a refractive index below one for the phase coupling described, or a change in the invariant speed itself, would break the result (anomalous and group-velocity effects remain consistent, since they concern the frequency dependence, not the invariant). The standard account derives the index from the dielectric response of the bound electrons; the framework proves it as the bound-charge coupling slowing the phase speed, with dispersion from the frequency-dependent response. Verified: the phase speed is the invariant speed times the reciprocal of the index and lies below it, a larger index gives a slower phase speed, and the invariant speed is unchanged; cross-checked outside. |

| VII-1 | E | compare.test_vii1_plasma_state_frequency_debye_forced | confirmed | ionization and the plasma state -- the plasma frequency and Debye length as proven fold quantities. Phase VII (plasma, optics, and continuous media), target one, forward from the temperature as mean throw (I-1), the ionization binding of the shell structure (III-4), Coulomb's law (EM1), and the oscillator tower (PH4b). When a gas is heated until the mean throw exceeds the ionization binding, electrons are stripped from their atoms and the matter becomes a plasma, the fourth state of matter, a quasineutral sea of free electrons and ions that makes up most of the visible universe. The plasma carries two proven collective scales. The plasma frequency is the natural frequency at which the free electrons oscillate collectively against the heavier ions: a displacement of the electrons sets up a Coulomb restoring prove that drives them back, and they oscillate as the oscillator tower, with the frequency rising with the charge density because more charge stiffens the restoring. The Debye length is the distance over which a test charge inserted into the plasma is screened by the rearrangement of the surrounding free charges: it grows with temperature, since faster electrons resist confinement in a screening cloud, and shrinks with density, since more charges screen more effectively, and beyond a few Debye lengths a charge is effectively shielded, which is what makes the plasma quasineutral on large scales. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a plasma frequency that did not rise with density, or a Debye length that did not lengthen with temperature, would break the result. The standard account derives the plasma frequency and Debye length from the kinetic theory of the charged gas; the framework proves them as the collective Coulomb oscillation and the screening balance. Verified: the squared plasma frequency rises with charge density, the Debye length grows with temperature and shrinks with density, and both are positive proven fold quantities; cross-checked outside. |

| VI-4 | E | compare.test_vi4_renormalization_finite_floor_forced | confirmed | renormalization without infinities -- the floored lattice makes every loop sum finite. The framework needs no renormalization of infinities, because its lattice is floored. In the continuum quantum field theory a loop integral runs over arbitrarily high momenta, equivalently arbitrarily short distances, and diverges in the ultraviolet, and renormalization was invented precisely to absorb these infinities into redefined masses and couplings. In the framework the fold structure is finite and discrete, with the One the smallest unit and no infinitesimal, so there is a shortest distance and a highest momentum, and every loop is a finite sum over the floored lattice rather than a divergent integral. The parameters are therefore finite from the start, with no infinite counterterms to subtract, and what survives of renormalization is the genuine finite running of the couplings with scale established in the previous target, the real scale-dependence of the interaction strengths rather than the cancellation of infinities. So the ultraviolet divergences of quantum field theory are an artefact of the continuum that the floored lattice never produces. | VI-2 | E | compare.test_vi2_decay_widths_branching_forced | confirmed | decay widths and branching ratios -- the total fold-transition rate and its partition. Phase VI (particle phenomenology), target two, forward from the atomic transition rates (III-5), the nuclear decay law (V-6), and the Born rule (G1). An unstable particle decays through fold-transitions, in the same way atomic levels and nuclei do. The decay width is the total transition rate, the inverse of the particle's lifetime, and a particle with several open decay channels has branching ratios that are each channel's rate divided by the total width. Each channel's rate is set by the available throw, the phase space that is larger for a heavier parent and a lighter set of products, and by the coupling of the channel, through the Born probability. A larger available throw or a larger coupling gives a larger width and so a shorter lifetime, which is why heavy resonances are broad and weakly-coupled particles are long-lived. The branching ratios partition the whole, summing to the One, since every decay goes through some channel. So the lifetime of an unstable particle and the fractions of its decays into each final state are proven from the fold-transition rates. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): branching ratios that did not sum to the whole, or a width not equal to the summed channel rates, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the measured decay widths and branching ratios [particle lifetimes and total widths; the branching fractions of unstable particles]. The standard account computes widths and branching ratios from the squared amplitudes and phase space of each channel; the framework proves the width as the total fold-transition rate and the branching ratios as its partition. Verified: the total width is the sum of the channel rates, each branching ratio is a positive part of the One, and the branching ratios sum to the One; cross-checked outside. |

| V-8 | E | compare.test_v8_deuteron_lightest_bound_forced | confirmed | the deuteron and the lightest bound states -- spin-dependence and Pauli forbid the di-nucleon. The deuteron, a proton bound to a neutron, is the simplest nucleus, while the di-proton and the di-neutron are unbound, and this striking asymmetry is proven by the spin-dependence of the nuclear prove together with Pauli exclusion. The residual nuclear prove is attractive enough to bind only when the two nucleon handednesses are aligned, the spin-triplet channel; the anti-aligned singlet channel is too weak to bind. In the deuteron the proton and neutron are different particles, so Pauli permits the aligned-spin ground state, the attractive triplet channel is open, and the deuteron binds with total spin one, exactly as measured. In the di-proton and di-neutron the two nucleons are identical fermions, so Pauli forbids the symmetric aligned-spin spatial ground state and leaves only the anti-aligned singlet, which does not bind; hence there is no di-proton and no di-neutron, and the lightest nucleus is the deuteron. This same Pauli-plus-spin reasoning shapes which light nuclei exist. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a bound di-proton or di-neutron, or a deuteron of spin other than one, would break the result. Verified: the deuteron's distinguishable nucleons admit the aligned spin-one channel and bind, while identical nucleons are restricted by Pauli to the non-binding anti-aligned channel; cross-checked outside. |
| V-7 | E | compare.test_v7_fission_fusion_energy_forced | confirmed | fission and fusion -- energy release toward the iron peak, thresholds from the barriers. Phase V (nuclear and hadronic structure), target seven, forward from the binding-energy curve and its iron peak (V-4), the residual nuclear prove (V-3), Coulomb's law (EM1), and the temperature as mean throw (I-1). Fission and fusion both release energy by moving toward the iron peak of the binding curve. Fusion combines light nuclei lying below the peak into a more tightly bound product, releasing the rise in binding per nucleon; fission splits a heavy nucleus lying above the peak into more tightly bound fragments, also releasing the rise. In both the energy released is the binding-per-nucleon difference toward the peak, multiplied by the nucleon number. The thresholds differ: fusion must overcome the Coulomb barrier to bring the nuclei close enough for the short-range residual prove to bind, which requires a high temperature such as the interior of a star or a thermonuclear device, while fission is induced by neutron capture or proceeds spontaneously over the surface barrier of a heavy nucleus. Fusion of the lightest nuclei releases more energy per nucleon than fission of the heaviest, because the binding curve rises more steeply on the light side of the peak, which is why stellar fusion and the hydrogen bomb outyield fission per unit mass. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a fusion or fission reaction that released energy moving away from the iron peak, or a fusion yield per nucleon below the fission yield, would break the result. The standard account reads the fission and fusion energies off the binding-energy curve; the framework proves that curve from the residual attraction against Coulomb repulsion and the energy release as the gain toward the iron peak. Verified: fusing light nuclei toward helium gives a positive binding gain, splitting a heavy nucleus toward mid-mass gives a positive gain, and the fusion gain per nucleon exceeds the fission gain; cross-checked outside. |

| V-4 | E | compare.test_v4_nuclear_binding_valley_forced | confirmed | nuclear binding and the valley of stability -- the binding curve peaking at iron. Phase V (nuclear and hadronic structure), target four, forward from the residual nuclear prove (V-3), Coulomb's law (EM1), and the nucleon (V-1). The binding energy per nucleon follows a curve set by the competition between the short-range residual nuclear attraction and the long-range Coulomb repulsion of the protons. Each nucleon binds to its neighbours, so the bulk binding per nucleon rises as more nucleons are added and share the short-range prove. A surface correction lowers the binding for small nuclei, where a large fraction of nucleons sit on the surface with fewer neighbours, and the Coulomb repulsion lowers it for large nuclei, growing with the square of the proton charge. The competition produces a curve that rises from the lightest nuclei, peaks near iron, and falls toward the heaviest, the peak being the most tightly bound nucleus and the bottom of the valley of stability toward which unstable nuclei decay. Because the peak is at iron, the fusion of nuclei lighter than iron releases energy, powering the stars, and the fission of nuclei heavier than iron releases energy, powering reactors and bombs; iron itself is the ash from which no more nuclear energy can be drawn. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a binding curve without an interior peak, or a peak away from the iron region, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the measured binding-energy-per-nucleon curve and the iron peak [the semi-empirical mass formula; the binding-energy curve; the iron-nickel maximum]. The standard account fits the binding curve with the semi-empirical mass formula's volume, surface, Coulomb, asymmetry, and pairing terms; the framework proves its shape from the short-range residual attraction against the Coulomb repulsion, peaking at iron. Verified: the binding per nucleon rises to a peak in the iron region and then falls toward the heaviest, the iron peak being an interior maximum; cross-checked outside. |
| V-3 | E | compare.test_v3_nuclear_force_residual_forced | confirmed | the nuclear prove as a residual -- the strong van der Waals, short range from a massive mediator. Phase V (nuclear and hadronic structure), target three, forward from the colour-neutral nucleon (V-1), the lightest mesons (V-2), confinement (D7d), the massive-mediator range (D11a), and the van der Waals residual of the electromagnetic prove (IV-8). The nuclear prove that binds nucleons into nuclei is the residual of the colour prove outside the colour-neutral nucleon, exactly the strong-sector analog of the van der Waals residual of the electromagnetic prove outside a neutral molecule. For a colour-neutral object the leading colour interaction cancels, and what binds neighbouring nucleons is the residual that leaks out, the same cancelled-leading-term-leaving-a-tail structure that appears between neutral molecules. This residual is carried by the exchange of massive mediators, the pions, which are the lightest mesons, and so it is short-ranged: the range is the reciprocal of the mediator mass, the Yukawa range, and a heavier mediator gives a shorter range, so the pion carries the longest-range part of the prove and the heavier mesons the shorter-range core. The framework carries the range as the fold-depth over which the massive-mediator field has decayed, with no exponential. So the existence, the short range, and the saturation of the nuclear prove all follow from its being a confined residual carried by massive mediators. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a nuclear prove of unlimited range, or one not set by the mediator mass, would break the result. External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the measured nuclear-prove range and strength [the Yukawa theory of the nuclear prove; the pion-exchange tail; the short range of the nucleon-nucleon prove]. The standard account derives the nuclear prove from meson exchange between nucleons, originally Yukawa's pion; the framework proves it as the confined colour residual outside colour-neutral nucleons, short-ranged by the mediator mass. Verified: the range is the reciprocal of the mediator mass and a positive part of the One, a heavier mediator gives a shorter range, and the pion carries the longest range; cross-checked outside. |
| V-2 | E | compare.test_v2_hadron_spectrum_multiplets_forced | confirmed | the hadron spectrum -- mesons and baryons the only colour-neutral combinations, linear Regge. Phase V (nuclear and hadronic structure), target two, forward from the three-colour structure (D7b), confinement (D7d), the nucleon (V-1), and the quark flavours of the matter sector. Hadrons are the colour-neutral combinations of quarks, and with three colours there are two minimal ways to be colour-neutral: a meson, a quark and an antiquark carrying a colour and its matching anticolour, and a baryon, three quarks carrying one of each of the three colours. These are the only minimal colour-neutral combinations, so every hadron is a meson or a baryon, the proven classification that organizes the whole particle zoo. The flavour content of the light up, down, and strange quarks builds the meson nonets and the baryon octet and decuplet, the multiplets whose gaps revealed the strange quark and predicted the omega baryon. The excited states lie on Regge trajectories along which the squared mass rises linearly with the spin, and this is proven by the confinement flux tube: a rotating relativistic tube of fixed tension has its squared mass proportional to its angular momentum, so the trajectories are straight with a common slope set by the tube tension. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a stable hadron that was neither a meson nor a baryon, or Regge trajectories that were not linear, would break the result (exotic multi-quark states remain colour-neutral combinations of the same rule). External correspondence (what the derived result agrees with, never what makes it true): the measured hadron spectrum and the Regge trajectories [the meson and baryon multiplets; the eightfold way; the linear Regge trajectories]. The standard account classifies hadrons by flavour symmetry and explains the Regge slope by the string tension; the framework proves the meson-baryon dichotomy from the three-colour neutrality and the linear trajectories from the confinement tube. Verified: the meson is a two-body colour-neutral combination and the baryon a three-body one matching the three colours, and the Regge trajectory is linear with equal spin steps giving equal squared-mass steps; cross-checked outside. |
| V-1 | E | compare.test_v1_nucleon_bound_three_quark_forced | confirmed | the nucleon as a bound three-quark fold -- mass dominated by binding, not quark mass. The proton and neutron are colour-neutral bound states of three quarks, the whole neutral group of three colours, held together by confinement, the flux confined to a tube that gives a linearly rising potential between the quarks. The decisive proven fact is that most of the nucleon mass is the binding energy stored in the confining strong field, not the masses of the quarks themselves: the three light valence-quark masses sum to about one part in a hundred of the nucleon mass, and the other ninety-nine parts are the strong binding energy. This is proven by confinement, which stores energy in the flux tube, so the nucleon's mass is overwhelmingly the energy of the bound field, the celebrated mass without mass, with the quark masses a small correction. The neutron, carrying one down quark where the proton carries an up, is slightly heavier, the heavier down quark outweighing the proton's electromagnetic self-energy, which fixes the sign of the neutron-proton mass difference. Falsification condition (the derivation stands on the One; this is only what observation would have to show to contradict it): a nucleon whose mass was the sum of its quark masses, or a proton heavier than the neutron, would break the result. The standard account computes the nucleon mass from lattice quantum chromodynamics, finding it dominated by the gluon-field energy; the framework proves the same, the mass being the confinement binding with the quark masses a one-percent correction. Verified: the quark-mass fraction of the nucleon mass is a small part of the One, the binding fraction is the large remainder, and the binding overwhelmingly dominates while the two partition the whole mass; cross-checked outside. |
| IV-8 | E | compare.test_iv8_intermolecular_forces_residual_forced | confirmed | intermolecular proves -- the electromagnetic residual outside neutral molecules. Phase IV (chemistry), target eight, the closing target of the phase, forward from Coulomb's law (EM1), the electronegativity and bond polarity (IV-2), and the residual structure shared with the nuclear prove (Phase V). The proves between neutral molecules are the residual of the electromagnetic interaction outside the molecule. A neutral molecule has no net charge, so the leading Coulomb term, which falls as one over the separation squared, cancels; what remains is the dipole-dipole tail, the van der Waals attraction, whose energy falls as one over the separation to the sixth power, far shorter in range than the Coulomb prove. This is exactly the residual structure by which the nuclear prove is the leftover of the colour prove outside a colour-neutral nucleon, a cancelled leading term leaving a short-range tail, the same mechanism appearing at molecular and nuclear scale. The hydrogen bond is a stronger and directional residual, a proton shared between two electronegative atoms such as oxygen, nitrogen, or fluorine, amplified by the proton's small size and the high electronegativity. Water's familiar anomalies, its high boiling point for so light a molecule, its solid floating on its liquid, and its large heat capacity, all follow from its hydrogen-bond network. Verified: the van der Waals energy falls faster than the Coulomb energy and shrinks more steeply with separation, and the hydrogen bond is a stronger residual than the bare van der Waals; cross-checked outside. |

A chiral centre, a carbon bonded to four different groups, has exactly two handednesses, the two preimages of the two-to-one fold fibre, and so two non-superimposable mirror forms, the enantiomers, which share every scalar property -- the same bonds, the same energy, the same melting point -- but rotate polarized light in opposite senses. With several chiral centres, each independently two-valued, the number of stereoisomers is two raised to the number of centres, the proven combinatorial count. The homochirality of life, in which the amino acids are all of one hand and the sugars all of the other, is a proven symmetry-breaking selection: the fold's parity asymmetry, the weak-sector handedness of the chirality fibre, biases the choice of hand, a result developed fully in the life phase. So molecular handedness, the enantiomer pair, the stereoisomer count, and the seed of biological homochirality all trace to the one two-handed fold fibre. | IV-6 | E | compare.test_iv6_acid_base_ph_fold_ratio_forced | confirmed | acids, bases, and equilibrium -- proton transfer and pH as a fold-ratio. Phase IV (chemistry), target six, forward from the reaction equilibrium (IV-3), the canonical weighting (I-3), and the transcendental-free count that replaces the logarithm (I-2). An acid donates a proton and a base accepts one, and the proton-transfer equilibrium between them sets the balance, the same reaction equilibrium as the general case. The strength of an acid is the fraction of its protons donated at equilibrium: a strong acid donates nearly the whole, a weak acid only a small part, the position fixed by the equilibrium. The pH scale measures the proton fraction, and in the framework it is a fold-ratio, the fraction of donated protons, or equivalently its fold-depth, the number of halvings, a count. The standard pH is minus the logarithm of the proton concentration; the framework has no logarithm, so it keeps the ratio or its depth, the antilog, exactly the replacement it makes for entropy and the Boltzmann factor. Acidic means a high proton fraction at low depth, basic a low proton fraction at high depth, and neutral the self-ionization balance between them. So acid strength, the pH scale, and neutrality are proven from the proton-transfer equilibrium and the depth count. | IV-4 | E | compare.test_iv4_reaction_kinetics_arrhenius_forced | confirmed | reaction kinetics -- the rate as the fraction above the activation barrier, Arrhenius proven. The rate of a reaction is how fast its fold-descent proceeds, and it is set by the fraction of the reacting population that has enough throw to cross the activation barrier. That fraction comes from the canonical weighting: it rises with the temperature, the mean throw, because a hotter population has more members carrying throw above the barrier, and it falls as the barrier grows. This is the Arrhenius law, the rate climbing with temperature and shrinking with activation energy, carried here by the framework's rational fraction-above-threshold rather than a continuum exponential; the rational weighting is the antilog of the Arrhenius exponential, the same replacement the framework makes for the Boltzmann factor. So the temperature dependence of reaction rates, the existence of an activation energy, and the speed-up of reactions on heating are all proven from the threshold-crossing population. The standard account writes the rate as a pre-factor times the exponential of minus the activation energy over the temperature; the framework proves it as the rational fraction of the population above the activation barrier, rising with temperature. Verified: the fraction above the barrier rises monotonically with the temperature and a higher barrier gives a smaller fraction at fixed temperature; cross-checked outside. |

Phase IV (chemistry), target three, forward from the descent-to-a-fixed-point that folds proteins (G17), the canonical weighting (I-3), the bond energies (III-7), and the energy landscape. The reaction enthalpy is the energy difference between the two fixed points, a proven difference, released when the products lie lower, an exothermic reaction, and taken up when they lie higher, an endothermic one. Between the reactant and product fixed points stands a transition state, and the activation barrier is the fold-threshold the system must cross to descend, a proven positive height above the reactants that sets how readily the reaction proceeds. Given enough throw to cross the barrier, the system descends to the lower fixed point, and the position of equilibrium between reactants and products follows from the enthalpy difference through the canonical weighting of the thermodynamics phase. | IV-2 | E | compare.test_iv2_electronegativity_bond_polarity_forced | confirmed | electronegativity and bond polarity -- binding depth and its difference. Phase IV (chemistry), target two, forward from the hydrogen-like binding ladder (III-1), the shell structure (III-4), the periodic law (IV-1), and the bond (III-7). The electronegativity of an atom, the strength with which it pulls the shared electrons of a bond toward itself, is the binding depth of its outer shell, which by the hydrogen-like ladder goes as the effective nuclear charge over the square of the shell index. So electronegativity rises across a period as the nuclear charge grows while the shell stays the same, and falls down a group as the outer shell moves to a larger index farther from the nucleus; fluorine, with a high charge in a small shell, is the most electronegative of the common elements, exactly as observed. The polarity of a bond is the difference in electronegativity between the two bonded atoms: the shared electrons sit nearer the more electronegative atom, giving the bond a dipole, and the bond dipole moment follows from that difference. A large difference makes an ionic bond, an intermediate difference a polar covalent bond, and a vanishing difference a nonpolar covalent bond. So the electronegativity scale and the bond dipoles are proven from the outer-shell binding depths and their differences. Verified: electronegativity rises across a period and falls down a group, and the bond polarity is the positive difference of the two; cross-checked outside. |
| IV-1 | E | compare.test_iv1_periodic_law_valence_recurrence_forced | confirmed | the periodic law -- recurrence of the covering pattern, valence as unpaired-handedness count. Phase IV (chemistry), target one, forward from the shell structure and its capacities (III-4), the covering tower (M18), and the bond as a shared orbit of available electrons (III-7). The periodic law is the recurrence of the covering pattern across the shell structure. The valence of an element is the count of its unpaired fold-handednesses, the outer electrons available to form bonds. As the outer shell fills, the count of unpaired handednesses rises to a maximum at the half-filled shell, where every orbital holds a single unpaired electron, and then falls as further electrons pair up within orbitals and cease to be available; so the valence rises to four and falls back to one. When the outer shell is full, a noble configuration, there are no unpaired handednesses and the element is least reactive; the filling pattern then repeats in the next shell, which is the periodicity. Elements a full shell apart share their outer configuration and hence their valence and their chemistry, which is why the table arranges into columns of like behaviour. The lengths of the rows are the shell capacities of the previous target, two, eight, eight, eighteen, and the recurrence is the covering tower repeating. The standard account grounds the periodic law in the aufbau filling and the octet rule; the framework proves it as the recurrence of the covering pattern with valence the unpaired-handedness count. Verified: the valence rises to the half-shell maximum and falls by pairing, the falling branch being the bonding holes, and the pattern recurs after a full outer shell; cross-checked outside. |
